Date: Tue, 12 Mar 2019 15:00:18 -0400
From: Eugene Surowitz <surow@verizon.net>
To: Tim Daly <axiomcas@gmail.com>
Subject: Re: [Axiom-developer] Scratchpad II Newsletters

The Scratchpad II Newsletter v.1 n.2 Sept 1 1985
appears to be a slightly earlier version than the copy I found
in a box of Scratchpad-ish literature I have.

I also found a copy of "Scratchpad User's Manual" dated June 1975!
Also have a copy of "Scratchpad / Technical Newsletter" 11/15/1975.

Ditto:

"MODLISP: A Preliminary Design" by Jenks dated 01/18/80 an IBM Research Report

"MODLISP" by Jenks and Davenport dated 10/29/80 an IBM Research Report

"A Language for Computer Algebra" by Jenks and Trager dated ACM 1981

Cheers, Gene

On 2/19/2019 4:50 AM, Tim Daly wrote:
> While re-organizing my library I came across a lot of historical documents
> for Scratchpad / Axiom. This first push is a set of Newsletters issued
> during the IBM Scratchpad II days. I've integrated them into the build.
> 
> More to come. Stay tuned.
> 
> Tim

\start
Date: Wed, 13 Mar 2019 14:49:33 -0400
From: Tim Daly <axiomcas@gmail.com>
To: Waldek Hebisch <hebisch@math.uni.wroc.pl>,
	axiom-dev <axiom-developer@nongnu.org>
Subject: [Axiom-developer] Request
Cc: Ralf Hemmecke <ralf@hemmecke.de>

https://groups.google.com/forum/#!topic/fricas-devel/v-S7_27s5gs

Fricas, which has maintained an active effort to remove and
block any attempts at documentation, now makes reference
to the Google Docs effort? Waldek, do you expect that someone
else would document the integration code?

The only possible way that this software can survive to the
next generation of developers will be deep documentation.
People, including yourself, find that they do not want to try
to understand the raw code, spad or lisp, without some help.

If the 6 people who are active in Fricas are unwilling or unable
to document, it seems unlikely that tech writers will be willing
to waste time on it.

I'm not an active supporter of Fricas, which is an understatement,
but I would like the open source version of our efforts to survive
and prosper, regardless of our differences.

Please make every effort to document everything.

Date: Mon, 25 Mar 2019 00:26:39 -0400
From: Tim Daly <axiomcas@gmail.com>
To: axiom-dev <axiom-developer@nongnu.org>
Subject: [Axiom-developer] Proving Axiom Sane [PAS]: Bagn19 paper

Roberto Bagnara, Abramo Bagnara, Fabio Biselli, Michele Chiari, and Roberta Gori
"Correct Approximation of IEEE 754 Floating-Point Arithmetic for
Program Verification"

an interesting read as well as a good example of using TAC (three-address code)
and SSA (static single assignment) in proofs. This allows constraint propagation
and constrained solutoins.

Well worth the read.

Tim

\start
Date: Fri, 29 Mar 2019 05:44:58 -0400
From: Tim Daly <axiomcas@gmail.com>
To: axiom-dev <axiom-developer@nongnu.org>
Subject: [Axiom-developer] Axiom on Windows 10

1) enable developer mode
https://www.ghacks.net/2015/06/13/how-to-enable-developer-mode-in-windows-10-to-sideload-apps/

2) run powershell as admin

3) type:
Enable-WindowsOptionalFeature -Online -FeatureName
Microsoft-Windows-Subsystem-Linux

4) visit the Windows store and download Ubuntu 16.04

5) run Ubuntu to install it

6) dowload axiom binary
http://axiom-developer.org/axiom-website/downloads/axiom-ubuntu64-may2017-bin.tgz

7) untar the axiom binary
cd Downloads
tar -zxf axiom-ubutu64-may2017-bin.tgz

8) cd to the ubuntu subdirectory
cd axiom/mnt/ubuntu

9) set up the shell variables
export AXIOM=`pwd`
export PATH=$AXIOM/bin:$PATH

10) run axiom
axiom

Note that Ubuntu under windows accesses Windows files using an mnt prefix
e.g. mnt/c/ is the C: drive

So Axiom runs on my linux, mac, windows, and android (my phone / tablet)

Tim

\start
Date: Fri, 29 Mar 2019 06:54:34 -0400
From: Tim Daly <axiomcas@gmail.com>
To: axiom-dev <axiom-developer@nongnu.org>
Subject: [Axiom-developer] Axiom on Windows 10 with HyperDoc

once Axiom is installed (see previous email) you can run axiom
with hyperdoc. Download and install VcXsrv on Windows:
https://sourceforge.net/projects/vcxsrv/

In order to run graphics you need to install gcc:
sudo apt-get install gcc

in your .profile file you can add three lines:
export AXIOM=.... path to axiom/mnt/ubuntu ....
export PATH=$AXIOM/bin:$PATH
export DISPLAY=localhost:0.0

Then when you type 'axiom', you get a hyperdoc window also.

Note that ubuntu can read windows files using /mnt/c/...pathToFile

Tim
